## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: classical mechanics — nonlinear oscillations & dynamical systems
**Analysis**: The target dv_dt is acceleration expressed as a function of position x, velocity v, and possibly explicit time t, which is the standard state-space form of (non)linear oscillators. Common physics mechanisms include restoring forces (linear/nonlinear), damping (linear/nonlinear), and external/parametric forcing (t-dependent terms).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Simple harmonic oscillator (undamped): dv_dt = -c0 * x (linear restoring force, energy-conserving)
- Linearly damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v (viscous damping proportional to velocity)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * cos(c3 * t) (external periodic forcing)
- Driven damped oscillator (sine drive): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (alternative phase convention)
- Duffing oscillator (cubic stiffness): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v (hardening/softening spring nonlinearity)
- Duffing with periodic drive: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (chaos/bi-stability regimes)
- Simple pendulum (nonlinear restoring): dv_dt = -c0 * sin(c1 * x) - c2 * v (large-angle restoring torque; c1 often 1 if x is angle)
- Quadratic (aerodynamic) damping: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * v * Abs(v) (drag scaling with speed squared)
- Coulomb/friction-like damping (smooth): dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * v - c2 * tanh(c3 * v) (dry friction approximated smoothly)
- Van der Pol oscillator (self-excited): dv_dt = -c0 * x + c1 * (c2 - x**2) * v (negative damping at small |x|, limit cycle)
- Rayleigh oscillator (velocity-nonlinear damping): dv_dt = -c0 * x + (c1 - c2 * v**2) * v (self-oscillation via v-dependent damping)
- Parametrically excited oscillator: dv_dt = -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x - c3 * v (time-varying stiffness; Mathieu-type behavior)
- Nonlinear stiffness with mixed terms: dv_dt = -c0 * x - c1 * x**3 - c2 * x**5 - c3 * v (higher-order elastic nonlinearities)
- Liénard-type general oscillator: dv_dt = -c0 * x - (c1 + c2 * x**2) * v (broad family capturing amplitude-dependent damping)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Conservative restoring force → dv_dt primarily a function of x (often odd in x): terms like -c * x, -c * sin(c * x), -c * x**3
- Viscous dissipation → linear damping term -c * v producing exponential energy decay in the absence of forcing
- Aerodynamic/large-Re drag → damping scales like -c * v * Abs(v), leading to faster decay at high speeds than linear damping
- Dry friction → nearly constant-magnitude opposing acceleration: -c * sign(v), often smoothed as -c * tanh(c * v) for differentiability
- Hardening/softening spring behavior → inclusion of -c * x**3 (and higher odd powers) causing amplitude-dependent frequency shifts
- Large-angle pendulum behavior → -c * sin(c * x) instead of -c * x, capturing nonlinear period increase with amplitude
- External periodic drive → additive forcing c * cos(c * t) or c * sin(c * t), creating resonance peaks and phase-locking regions
- Parametric resonance → stiffness modulation -(c0 + c1 * cos(c2 * t)) * x, enabling growth near twice the natural frequency
- Self-excited limit cycles → “negative damping” at small amplitude but positive at large amplitude, e.g., (c0 - x**2)*v or (c0 - v**2)*v

GT Equivalence Verification (PO7)
============================================================
GT: -alpha*v**c0 - beta*Abs(v)**c1 - omega0**c2*x**c3
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT:** `-0.0458938827292319*v**3 - 1.28311219603499*x**3 - 0.729560991204844*Abs(v)**0.333333333333333`

The GT has three terms:
1. A `v**3` term
2. An `x**3` term  
3. An `|v|^(1/3)` term

The critical issue is the `Abs(v)` term. Since `v` takes both positive and negative values, `|v|^(1/3)` is NOT equivalent to `v^(1/3)` (which would be complex for negative v in many conventions, or `-|v|^{1/3}$` in real arithmetic).

For a candidate to match, it needs:
- An `x**3` term
- A `v**3` term
- An `|v|^(1/3)` term (or equivalent)
- All other terms must be eliminable (set to zero)

**Key problem:** None of the candidates contain `Abs(v)`. They use `v**c` terms. The expression `v**c3` where c3=1/3 is problematic for negative v. In standard real-valued math, `v^(1/3)` for negative v gives `-|v|^(1/3)`, which is an odd function, while `|v|^(1/3)` is an even function. These are fundamentally different.

However, let me check: can any combination of terms produce `|v|^(1/3)`? 

For candidates with `log` terms: `log(c*v + 1)` cannot produce `|v|^{1/3}`.
For candidates with `exp` terms: `exp(c*v)` cannot produce `|v|^{1/3}`.
For candidates with `sin` terms: `sin` cannot produce `|v|^{1/3}`.

The only way to get `|v|^{1/3}` from power terms would be if we interpret `v**c` as `|v|^c` (which some symbolic regression frameworks do), but the candidates are written symbolically as `v**c3`, not `Abs(v)**c3`.

Given the domain constraints explicitly state that `v` takes both signs and `Abs(v)` is NOT equivalent to `v` or `-v`, the `|v|^{1/3}` term cannot be reproduced by `v^{1/3}` since they differ for negative v.

**None of the candidates contain `Abs(v)`**, so none can exactly reproduce the `|v|^{1/3}` term.

Let me verify this conclusion by checking each candidate systematically. Every candidate uses `v**c` (not `Abs(v)**c`), `log`, `exp`, or `sin` of `v`. None of these can produce `|v|^{1/3}` which is an even function of `v` raised to a fractional power.

Even combinations like `v^a + v^b` for various a, b cannot produce `|v|^{1/3}` because power functions of v (with real exponents, assuming standard real-valued interpretation) produce odd or even functions depending on the exponent, but `|v|^{1/3}` specifically requires the absolute value.

Therefore, **no candidate matches**.
